							<div class="mw-indicators">

					<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content"><div class="mw-subjectpageheader">
</div><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Privacy-focused online search engine</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1320445320">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the search engine. For the children's game, see <a href="/wiki/Duck,_duck,_goose" title="Duck, duck, goose">Duck, duck, goose</a>. For the browser, see <a href="/wiki/DuckDuckGo_Private_Browser" title="DuckDuckGo Private Browser">DuckDuckGo Private Browser</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>

language)">Python</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>DuckDuckGo</b> is an American software company focused on <a href="/wiki/Internet_privacy" title="Internet privacy">online privacy</a> whose <a href="/wiki/Flagship_product" class="mw-redirect" title="Flagship product">flagship product</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Search_engine" title="Search engine">search engine</a> named DuckDuckGo. Founded by Gabriel Weinberg in 2008, its later products include <a href="/wiki/Browser_extension" title="Browser extension">browser extensions</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-extensions&#95;9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-extensions-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and a <a href="/wiki/DuckDuckGo_Private_Browser" title="DuckDuckGo Private Browser">custom DuckDuckGo web browser</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-private&#95;browser&#95;10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-private_browser-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Paoli,_Pennsylvania" title="Paoli, Pennsylvania">Paoli, Pennsylvania</a>, DuckDuckGo is a <a href="/wiki/Privately_held_company" title="Privately held company">privately held company</a> with about 200 employees.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The company's name is a reference to the children's game <a href="/wiki/Duck,_duck,_goose" title="Duck, duck, goose">duck, duck, goose</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-WashPostNov2012&#95;12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WashPostNov2012-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DuckDuckGo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Early_years">Early years</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DuckDuckGo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early years"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>DuckDuckGo was founded by Gabriel Weinberg and launched on February 29, 2008, in <a href="/wiki/Valley_Forge,_Pennsylvania" title="Valley Forge, Pennsylvania">Valley Forge, Pennsylvania</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-About&#95;6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-History&#95;14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Weinberg is an entrepreneur who previously launched <a href="/wiki/Names_Database" title="Names Database">Names Database</a>, a now-defunct social network. Self-funded by Weinberg until October 2011, DuckDuckGo was then "backed by <a href="/wiki/Union_Square_Ventures" title="Union Square Ventures">Union Square Ventures</a> and a handful of <a href="/wiki/Angel_investor" title="Angel investor">angel investors</a>."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-History&#95;14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Burnham13Oct11&#95;16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Burnham13Oct11-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Union Square partner Brad Burnham stated, "We invested in DuckDuckGo because we became convinced that it was not only possible to change the basis of competition in search, it was time to do it."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-History&#95;14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Burnham13Oct11&#95;16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Burnham13Oct11-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In addition, <a href="/wiki/Trisquel" title="Trisquel">Trisquel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Linux_Mint" title="Linux Mint">Linux Mint</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Midori_(web_browser)" title="Midori (web browser)">Midori</a> <a href="/wiki/Web_browser" title="Web browser">web browser</a> switched to use DuckDuckGo as their default search engine.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> DuckDuckGo gains revenue via advertisements and affiliate programs.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Search_engine" title="Search engine">search engine</a> is written in <a href="/wiki/Perl" title="Perl">Perl</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and runs on <a href="/wiki/Nginx" title="Nginx">nginx</a>, <a href="/wiki/FreeBSD" title="FreeBSD">FreeBSD</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Buys&#95;7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Buys-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-About&#95;6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> DuckDuckGo is built primarily upon search <a href="/wiki/API" title="API">APIs</a> from various vendors. As a result, <a href="/wiki/TechCrunch" title="TechCrunch">TechCrunch</a> characterized the service as a "hybrid" search engine.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-TCFriday&#95;21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCFriday-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Weinberg explained the beginnings of the name with respect to the children's game duck, duck, goose. He said of the origin of the name: "Really it just popped in my head one day and I just liked it. It is certainly influenced/derived from duck, duck, goose, but other than that there is no relation, e.g., a metaphor."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> DuckDuckGo was featured on TechCrunch's <a href="/wiki/Elevator_pitch" title="Elevator pitch">Elevator Pitch</a> Friday in 2008,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-TCFriday&#95;21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCFriday-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and it was a finalist in the 2008 <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!_Search_BOSS" class="mw-redirect" title="Yahoo! Search BOSS">BOSS</a> <a href="/wiki/Mashable" title="Mashable">Mashable</a> Challenge.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2010, DuckDuckGo began using privacy to differentiate itself from its competitors.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2010, Weinberg started a DuckDuckGo community website (duck.co) to allow the public to report problems, discuss means of spreading the use of the search engine, request features, and discuss <a href="/wiki/Open-sourcing" class="mw-redirect" title="Open-sourcing">open sourcing</a> the code.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The company registered the <a href="/wiki/Domain_name" title="Domain name">domain name</a> <i>ddg<a href="/wiki/.gg" title=".gg">.gg</a></i> on February 22, 2011,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and acquired <i>duck.com</i> in December 2018,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-duck.com&#95;30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-duck.com-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> which are used as shortened URL aliases that redirect to <i>duckduckgo.com</i>, and is also used as the domain for their email protection service.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Growth_in_the_2010s">Growth in the 2010s</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DuckDuckGo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Growth in the 2010s"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1224211176">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:.5em 1.4em .8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:.5em 0 .8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{overflow:hidden;position:relative;margin:.5em auto .8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft span,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright span{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox>blockquote{margin:0;padding:0;border-left:0;font-family:inherit;font-size:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{text-align:center;font-size:110%;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote>:first-child{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote:last-child>:last-child{margin-bottom:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" “ ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" ” ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .quote-title,.mw-parser-output .quotebox .quotebox-quote{display:block}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:640px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{width:100%!important;margin:0 0 .8em!important;float:none!important}}</style><div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:30%; ;">
<blockquote class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">
<p>We didn't invest in it because we thought it would beat Google. We invested in it because there is a need for a private search engine. We did it for the Internet anarchists, people that hang out on <a href="/wiki/Reddit" title="Reddit">Reddit</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hacker_News" title="Hacker News">Hacker News</a>.
</p>
</blockquote>
<div style="padding-bottom: 0; padding-top: 0.5em"><cite class="left-aligned" style="">— <a href="/wiki/Fred_Wilson_(financier)" title="Fred Wilson (financier)">Fred Wilson</a>, 2012 <a href="/wiki/TechCrunch_Disrupt" class="mw-redirect" title="TechCrunch Disrupt">TechCrunch Disrupt</a> Conference in New York<sup id="cite&#95;ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></cite></div>
</div><p>
By May 2012, the search engine was attracting 1.5 million searches a day. Weinberg reported that it had earned <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$115,000</span> in revenue in 2011 and had three employees, plus a small number of contractors.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Compete.com" title="Compete.com">Compete.com</a> estimated 266,465 unique visitors to the site in February 2012.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On April 12, 2011, <a href="/wiki/Alexa_Internet" title="Alexa Internet">Alexa</a> reported a 3-month growth rate of 51%.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> DuckDuckGo's own <a href="/wiki/Traffic_statistics" class="mw-redirect" title="Traffic statistics">traffic statistics</a> show that in August 2012 there were 1,393,644 visits per day, up from an average of 39,406 visits per day in April 2010 (the earliest data available).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In a lengthy profile in November 2012, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i> indicated that searches on DuckDuckGo numbered up to 45,000,000 per month in October 2012. The article concluded:</p><blockquote>
<p>"Weinberg's non-ambitious goals make him a particularly odd and dangerous competitor online. He can do almost everything that <a href="/wiki/Google_Search" title="Google Search">Google</a> or <a href="/wiki/Bing_(search_engine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bing (search engine)">Bing</a> can't because it could damage their business models, and if users figure out that they like the DuckDuckGo way better, Weinberg could damage the big boys without even really trying. It's asymmetrical digital warfare, and his backers at Union Square Ventures say Google is vulnerable."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-WashPostNov2012&#95;12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WashPostNov2012-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
</blockquote>
<p><a href="/wiki/GNOME" title="GNOME">GNOME</a> released <a href="/wiki/GNOME_Web" title="GNOME Web">Web</a> 3.10 on September 26, 2013, and starting with this version, the default search engine is DuckDuckGo.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>At its keynote speech at WWDC 2014 on September 18, 2014, Apple announced that DuckDuckGo would be included as a search option in both <a href="/wiki/IOS_8" title="IOS 8">iOS 8</a> and <a href="/wiki/OS_X_Yosemite" title="OS X Yosemite">OS X Yosemite</a> in its <a href="/wiki/Safari_(web_browser)" title="Safari (web browser)">Safari</a> browser.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On March 10, the <a href="/wiki/Pale_Moon" title="Pale Moon">Pale Moon</a> web browser, starting with version 24.4.0, included DuckDuckGo as its default search engine, as well as listed it on the browser's homepage.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In May 2014, DuckDuckGo released a redesigned version to beta testers through DuckDuckHack.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On May 21, 2014, DuckDuckGo officially released the redesigned version that focused on smarter answers and a more refined look. The new version added many new features, such as images, <a href="/wiki/Local_search_(Internet)" title="Local search (Internet)">local search</a>, auto-suggest, weather, recipes, and more.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On November 10, 2014, <a href="/wiki/Mozilla" title="Mozilla">Mozilla</a> added DuckDuckGo as a search option to <a href="/wiki/Firefox_33" class="mw-redirect" title="Firefox 33">Firefox 33.1</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On May 30, 2016, <a href="/wiki/The_Tor_Project" title="The Tor Project">The Tor Project, Inc</a> made DuckDuckGo the default search engine for <a href="/wiki/Tor_(network)#Tor_Browser" title="Tor (network)">Tor Browser</a> 6.0.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2016, DuckDuckGo officially announced the extension of its partnership with <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!_Search" class="mw-redirect" title="Yahoo! Search">Yahoo!</a> that brought new features to all users of the search engine, including date filtering of results and additional site links. It also partners with <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Bing" title="Microsoft Bing">Bing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yandex" title="Yandex">Yandex</a>, and Wikipedia to produce results or to use their features. The company also confirmed that it does not share user information with partner companies, as has always been its policy.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2018, it was reported that Google transferred ownership of the domain name Duck.com to DuckDuckGo. It is not known what price, if any, DuckDuckGo paid for the domain name.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-duck.com&#95;30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-duck.com-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On January 15, 2019, DuckDuckGo announced that all map and address-related searches would be powered by <a href="/wiki/Apple_Maps" title="Apple Maps">Apple Maps</a>, both on <a href="/wiki/Desktop_computer" title="Desktop computer">desktop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mobile_device" title="Mobile device">mobile devices</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2019, Google added DuckDuckGo to the default search engine list in <a href="/wiki/Google_Chrome" title="Google Chrome">Chrome</a> 73.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Beginning in 2018,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> the company has offered <a href="/wiki/Browser_extension" title="Browser extension">browser extensions</a> for popular <a href="/wiki/Web_browser" title="Web browser">web browsers</a> (<a href="/wiki/Google_Chrome" title="Google Chrome">Google Chrome</a>, <a href="/wiki/Safari_(web_browser)" title="Safari (web browser)">Safari</a>, and others).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-extensions&#95;9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-extensions-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The company also launched its own web browser, called the <a href="/wiki/DuckDuckGo_Private_Browser" title="DuckDuckGo Private Browser">DuckDuckGo Private Browser</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-private&#95;browser&#95;10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-private_browser-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Both of these products have protections against <a href="/wiki/Web_tracking" title="Web tracking">web tracking</a> and other privacy intrusions for all web browsing (not limited to DuckDuckGo searches).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Before August 2022, DuckDuckGo Private Browser did not block Microsoft tracking scripts.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-allows&#95;56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allows-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-caught&#95;57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-caught-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-pushback&#95;58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pushback-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="2020s">2020s</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DuckDuckGo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2020s"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In July 2021, DuckDuckGo introduced its <a href="/wiki/Email_forwarding" title="Email forwarding">email forwarding</a> feature, Email Protection, which lets users claim an "@duck.com" email address generated by the service. That inbox will receive emails, strip them of data trackers, and forward them to the user's private email address. The feature launched in beta for users of DuckDuckGo Private Browser on iOS and Android.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>As of March&#160;2022<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=DuckDuckGo&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, DuckDuckGo handled 102,704,358 daily searches on average.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-DDG-traffic&#95;60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DDG-traffic-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Also in April, DuckDuckGo said that they would protect users from being tracked by Google's <a href="/wiki/Accelerated_Mobile_Pages" title="Accelerated Mobile Pages">Accelerated Mobile Pages framework</a>, stating: "When you load or share a Google AMP page anywhere from DuckDuckGo apps (<a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a>/<a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a>/<a href="/wiki/MacOS" title="MacOS">MacOS</a>) or extensions (<a href="/wiki/Firefox" title="Firefox">Firefox</a>/<a href="/wiki/Google_Chrome" title="Google Chrome">Chrome</a>), the original publisher's webpage will be used in place of the Google AMP version".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2022, <a href="/wiki/Debian" title="Debian">Debian</a> package maintainers switched the default search engine in <a href="/wiki/Chromium_(web_browser)" title="Chromium (web browser)">Chromium</a> to DuckDuckGo for privacy reasons.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2024, DuckDuckGo introduced Privacy Pro. This paid subscription includes a <a href="/wiki/VPN" class="mw-redirect" title="VPN">VPN</a>, Personal Information Removal, and Identity Theft Restoration.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The subscription launched to users of the DuckDuckGo browser in the United States.
</p><p>Throughout 2025, DuckDuckGo rolled out a series of Easter eggs featuring <a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence_visual_art" title="Artificial intelligence visual art">AI-generated</a> images of Dax (DuckDuckGo's duck mascot) dressed up as characters from popular culture (or on 2 occasions replaced by them) when users search for the respective characters. There are currently 661 discovered variants of pop culture logos.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Features">Features</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DuckDuckGo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Features"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Privacy">Privacy</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DuckDuckGo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Privacy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>DuckDuckGo does not track its users.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> DuckDuckGo keeps <a href="/wiki/Favicon" title="Favicon">favicons</a> anonymous.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> User locations are never sent to DuckDuckGo servers, even when they allow a third party to collect their geolocations.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> DuckDuckGo offers limited third-party tracking protection, third-party cookie protection, CNAME cloaking protection, limited device <a href="/wiki/Fingerprint_(computing)" title="Fingerprint (computing)">fingerprint</a> protection from third parties, link tracking removal, Google AMP replacement, and do-not-track requests.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Search_results">Search results</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DuckDuckGo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Search results"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>DuckDuckGo's results are a compilation of "over 400" sources according to itself, including Bing, Yahoo! Search BOSS, <a href="/wiki/Wolfram_Alpha" class="mw-redirect" title="Wolfram Alpha">Wolfram Alpha</a>, Yandex, and its own <a href="/wiki/Web_crawler" title="Web crawler">web crawler</a> (the DuckDuckBot); but none from Google.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Buys&#95;7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Buys-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Hollingsworth-2019&#95;72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hollingsworth-2019-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-nyt&#95;mar2022&#95;73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt_mar2022-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It also uses data from <a href="/wiki/Crowdsourcing" title="Crowdsourcing">crowdsourced</a> sites such as <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia" title="Wikipedia">Wikipedia</a>, to populate knowledge panel boxes to the right of the search results.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Hollingsworth-2019&#95;72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hollingsworth-2019-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> During a Bing API outage in 2024, DuckDuckGo stopped showing results, indicating that Bing provided a substantial portion of DuckDuckGo's results.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>DuckDuckGo offers <i>HTML</i> and <i>lite</i> versions of its search for browsers without <a href="/wiki/JavaScript" title="JavaScript">JavaScript</a> capabilities.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>DuckDuckGo has refined the quality of its search engine results by deleting search results for companies they believe are <a href="/wiki/Content_farm" title="Content farm">content mills</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/EHow" title="EHow">eHow</a>, which publishes 4,000 articles per day produced by paid freelance writers, which Weinberg states to be "low-quality content designed specifically to rank highly in Google's search index". DuckDuckGo also filters pages with substantial advertising.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> DuckDuckGo down ranks websites deemed to have low journalistic standards.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Instant_Answers">Instant Answers</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DuckDuckGo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Instant Answers"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In addition to the indexed search results, DuckDuckGo displays relevant results, called <a href="/wiki/Instant_answer" title="Instant answer">instant answers</a>, at the top of the search page. These <b>Instant Answers</b> are collected from third-party APIs or static data sources such as text files. The Instant Answers are called <i>zeroclickinfo</i> because the intention behind these is to provide what users are searching for on the search result page itself, so that they do not have to click any results to find what they are looking for. Instant answers are created by and maintained by a community of over 1,500 open source contributors. This community has come to be known as DuckDuckHack.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-DuckDuckHack&#95;80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DuckDuckHack-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As of July 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=DuckDuckGo&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, there were 1,236 Instant Answers active.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In the DuckDuckHack documentation, four types of Instant Answers are described: <i>Goodies, Spices, Fatheads,</i> and <i>Longtails</i>. These types of Instant Answer extensions are differentiated by how their data is retrieved. Goodies do not retrieve data from a third-party API, whereas Spices do. Goodies instead use some form of the aforementioned static data sources, such as text files or <a href="/wiki/JSON" title="JSON">JSON</a> files. Fathead Instant Answers are key-value answers hosted on DuckDuckGo's <a href="/wiki/Back-end_database" title="Back-end database">backend</a>. Fathead key-value pairs function like a trigger to display the corresponding Instant Answer. Longtail Instant Answers are full-text queries to a DuckDuckGo database of articles. Paragraphs or snippets from any matching articles are returned, and the section that matches the user's query is highlighted.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2023, DuckDuckGo added <b>Search Assist</b> (formerly known as <b>DuckAssist</b>) to Instant Answers. Using <a href="/wiki/Large_language_model" title="Large language model">large language models</a> from <a href="/wiki/OpenAI" title="OpenAI">OpenAI</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anthropic" title="Anthropic">Anthropic</a>, Search Assist generates answers to users' questions by scanning online encyclopedias (like Wikipedia and <a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica" title="Encyclopædia Britannica">Britannica</a>).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Users can choose how often they want it to appear: Never, On-demand (only when Assist is clicked), Sometimes (when highly relevant), or Often (on a wide range of searches).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Search Assist is only available in a subset of English-speaking regions. Search Assist results also contain a "More" button, which allows users to have the AI generate a longer answer, and a button which allows users to ask a follow-up question using DuckDuckGo's AI chatbot, Duck.ai (more below)
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Tor_access"><span class="anchor" id="The&#95;onion&#95;service"></span>Tor access</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DuckDuckGo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Tor access"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In August 2010, DuckDuckGo introduced anonymous searching, including an exit enclave,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> for its search engine traffic using <a href="/wiki/Tor_(network)" title="Tor (network)">Tor network</a> and enabling access through a "Tor hidden service" (<a href="/wiki/Onion_service" class="mw-redirect" title="Onion service">onion service</a>).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <i><span style="word-break: break-all">3g2upl4pq6kufc4m.onion <span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/Tor_(network)" title="Tor network"><img alt="Tor network" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Tor-logo-2011-flat.svg/20px-Tor-logo-2011-flat.svg.png" decoding="async" width="18" height="11" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Tor-logo-2011-flat.svg/40px-Tor-logo-2011-flat.svg.png 1.5x" data-file-width="306" data-file-height="185" /></a></span></span><sup>(<a href="/wiki/Tor_(network)#Tor_Browser" title="Tor (network)">Accessing link help</a>)</sup></i><sup id="cite&#95;ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> (deprecated) was the DuckDuckGo v2 onion service on Tor.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This allows anonymity by routing traffic through a series of encrypted relays. Weinberg stated, "I believe this fits right in line with our privacy policy. Using Tor and DDG, you can now be end-to-end anonymous with your searches. And if you use our encrypted homepage, you can be end-to-end encrypted as well."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2021, DuckDuckGo introduced a new v3 onion service, with a new link: <i><span style="word-break: break-all">duckduckgogg42xjoc72x3sjasowoarfbgcmvfimaftt6twagswzczad.onion <span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/Tor_(network)" title="Tor network"><img alt="Tor network" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Tor-logo-2011-flat.svg/20px-Tor-logo-2011-flat.svg.png" decoding="async" width="18" height="11" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Tor-logo-2011-flat.svg/40px-Tor-logo-2011-flat.svg.png 1.5x" data-file-width="306" data-file-height="185" /></a></span></span><sup>(<a href="/wiki/Tor_(network)#Tor_Browser" title="Tor (network)">Accessing link help</a>)</sup></i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Bangs">Bangs</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DuckDuckGo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Bangs"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>DuckDuckGo includes "!Bang" keywords, which let users search specific third-party websites using the site's own search engine, if applicable. As of August 2020, 13,564 "bangs" for a diverse range of internet sites are available.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In December 2018, around 2,000 "bangs" were deleted. Some of them were deleted because they were broken, while others, such as searches for pirated content sites, were deleted for liability reasons.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Duck.ai">Duck.ai</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DuckDuckGo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Duck.ai"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><b>Duck.ai</b> (formerly known as <b>DuckDuckGo AI Chat</b>) is an opt-in <a href="/wiki/Chatbot" title="Chatbot">chatbot</a> that enables users to interact anonymously and privately with multiple <a href="/wiki/Large_language_models" class="mw-redirect" title="Large language models">large language models</a> (LLMs).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Introduced as a <a href="/wiki/Freemium" title="Freemium">freemium</a> service in June 2024 and exiting beta in March 2025,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Duck.ai provides free access to models including <a href="/wiki/OpenAI" title="OpenAI">OpenAI</a>'s <a href="/wiki/GPT-4o" title="GPT-4o">GPT-4o</a> mini, <a href="/wiki/GPT-5" title="GPT-5">GPT-5</a> mini and <a href="/wiki/GPT-OSS" class="mw-redirect" title="GPT-OSS">GPT-OSS</a> 120B, <a href="/wiki/Anthropic" title="Anthropic">Anthropic</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Claude_(language_model)" title="Claude (language model)">Claude</a> 3.5 Haiku, <a href="/wiki/Meta_Platforms" title="Meta Platforms">Meta</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Llama_(language_model)" title="Llama (language model)">Llama</a> 4 Scout, and <a href="/wiki/Mistral_AI" title="Mistral AI">Mistral AI</a>'s Mistral Small 3, while users with the DuckDuckGo subscription can receive higher usage limits and access advanced models including GPT-4o, <a href="/wiki/GPT-5.1" title="GPT-5.1">GPT-5.1</a>, Claude Sonnet 4.5, and Llama 4 Maverick as of December 2025. DuckDuckGo states that conversations within Duck.ai are stored locally on the user's device, and that prompts and outputs are not retained for model training because all data sent to providers is anonymized.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>100<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Users can disable Duck.ai along with Search Assist.
</p><p><b>Duck.ai Image Gen</b> is a feature that allows users to create AI-generated images by entering descriptive prompts. Generated images are stored locally on users' devices, with <a href="/wiki/Content_Authenticity_Initiative" title="Content Authenticity Initiative">C2PA</a>-compliant metadata for verification.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>101<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The feature exited beta in January 2026. The optional ability to add reference images was added.
</p><p>Voice chat was also added to Duck.ai in January 2026.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>102<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Business_model">Business model</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DuckDuckGo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Business model"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>DuckDuckGo earns revenue by serving ads primarily from the Yahoo-Bing search alliance network.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>103<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As a privacy-focused search engine, the ads served on DuckDuckGo are based on keywords and terms of the search query.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>104<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>105<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As of April 2024, DuckDuckGo also makes money from subscription fees paid to access Privacy Pro.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Donations">Donations</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DuckDuckGo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Donations"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The company supports charitable organizations that work to improve privacy; in 2021, they donated <a href="/wiki/US$" class="mw-redirect" title="US$">US$</a>1 million to these causes and had donated $3,650,000 over the previous decade. Major donations for 2021 included $200,000 to the <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Information_Technology_Policy" title="Center for Information Technology Policy">Center for Information Technology Policy</a>, $150,000 to the <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Frontier_Foundation" title="Electronic Frontier Foundation">Electronic Frontier Foundation</a>, $75,000 to <a href="/wiki/European_Digital_Rights" title="European Digital Rights">European Digital Rights</a> (EDRi) and $75,000 to <a href="/wiki/The_Markup" title="The Markup">The Markup</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>106<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Source_code">Source code</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DuckDuckGo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Source code"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Some of DuckDuckGo's <a href="/wiki/Source_code" title="Source code">source code</a> is <a href="/wiki/Free_and_open-source_software" title="Free and open-source software">free and open-source software</a> hosted at <a href="/wiki/GitHub" title="GitHub">GitHub</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Apache_License" title="Apache License">Apache 2.0 License</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>107<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>. Still, the core is <a href="/wiki/Proprietary_software" title="Proprietary software">proprietary</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>108<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> DuckDuckGo also hosted DuckDuckHack, a sister site for organizing open source contributions and community projects. The search engine's <a href="/wiki/Instant_answer" title="Instant answer">Instant Answers</a> are open source<sup id="cite&#95;ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>109<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and are maintained on GitHub, where anyone can view the source code. As of August 31, 2017, DuckDuckHack was placed in maintenance mode; as such, only <a href="/wiki/Pull_requests" class="mw-redirect" title="Pull requests">pull requests</a> for bug fixes will be approved.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-DuckDuckHack&#95;80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DuckDuckHack-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The date mentioned in this sentence was more than 7 years ago as of the date this template was added. (December 2024)">needs update</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Reception">Reception</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DuckDuckGo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Reception"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In a June 2011 article, Harry McCracken of <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> commended DuckDuckGo, comparing it to his favorite hamburger restaurant, <a href="/wiki/In-N-Out_Burger" title="In-N-Out Burger">In-N-Out Burger</a>:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1244412712">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 32px}.mw-parser-output .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;margin-top:0}@media(min-width:500px){.mw-parser-output .templatequotecite{padding-left:1.6em}}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>It feels a lot like early Google, with a stripped-down home page. Just as In-N-Out doesn't have lattes or Asian salads or sundaes or scrambled eggs, DDG doesn't try to do news or blogs or books or images. There's no auto-completion or instant results. It just offers core Web search—mostly the "ten blue links" approach that's still really useful, no matter what its critics say ... As for the quality, I'm not saying that Weinberg has figured out a way to return more relevant results than Google's mighty search team. But DuckDuckGo ... is really good at bringing back useful sites. It all feels meaty and straightforward and filler-free ...<sup id="cite&#95;ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>110<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></p></blockquote><p> The bare-bones approach cited in his quote has since changed; for instance, in 2014 DuckDuckGo added <a href="/wiki/Autocomplete" title="Autocomplete">auto-completion</a>, images, weather and more.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>111<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> McCracken included the site in <i>Time</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s list of "50 Best Websites of 2011."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>112<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Thom Holwerda, who reviewed the search engine for <a href="/wiki/OSNews" title="OSNews">OSNews</a>, praised its privacy features and shortcuts to site-specific searches as well as criticizing Google for "tracking pretty much everything you do", particularly because of the risk of such information being subject to a <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States" title="Federal government of the United States">U.S. government</a> <a href="/wiki/Subpoena" title="Subpoena">subpoena</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2012, in response to accusations that it was a monopoly, <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> identified DuckDuckGo as a competitor. Weinberg was reportedly "pleased and entertained" by that acknowledgment.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-WashPostNov2012&#95;12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WashPostNov2012-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2019, Twitter CEO <a href="/wiki/Jack_Dorsey" title="Jack Dorsey">Jack Dorsey</a> revealed his preference for using the DuckDuckGo search engine rather than Google, stating, "I love @DuckDuckGo. My default search engine for a while now. The app is even better!".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>114<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Conservative political commentators <a href="/wiki/Ben_Shapiro" title="Ben Shapiro">Ben Shapiro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dan_Bongino" title="Dan Bongino">Dan Bongino</a> have also endorsed DuckDuckGo.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Thompson-2022&#95;115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thompson-2022-115"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Controversies">Controversies</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DuckDuckGo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Controversies"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Censorship_allegations">Censorship allegations</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DuckDuckGo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Censorship allegations"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>On March 1, 2022, in response to the <a href="/wiki/Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian invasion of Ukraine">Russian invasion of Ukraine</a>, DuckDuckGo paused its partnership with <a href="/wiki/Yandex_Search" title="Yandex Search">Yandex Search</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Weinberg said in a tweet that DuckDuckGo will down-rank sites associated with Russian disinformation, a move which some users criticized as censorship and a violation of the search engine's commitment to "unbiased search." DuckDuckGo has defended itself from the criticism, saying that "The primary utility of a search engine is to provide access to accurate information. Disinformation sites that deliberately put out false information to intentionally mislead people directly cut against that utility."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>117<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>118<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-nyt&#95;mar2022&#95;73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt_mar2022-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Blocking_pirating_websites">Blocking pirating websites</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DuckDuckGo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Blocking pirating websites"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In April 2022, <a href="/wiki/TorrentFreak" title="TorrentFreak">TorrentFreak</a> reported that DuckDuckGo had blocked search results for some major <a href="/wiki/Online_piracy" title="Online piracy">pirating websites</a>, including <a href="/wiki/The_Pirate_Bay" title="The Pirate Bay">The Pirate Bay</a>, <a href="/wiki/1337x" title="1337x">1337x</a> and <a href="/wiki/FMovies" title="FMovies">FMovies</a>, as well as video downloading software <a href="/wiki/Youtube-dl" title="Youtube-dl">Youtube-dl</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Fingas-2022&#95;120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fingas-2022-120"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>120<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In a statement to <i><a href="/wiki/Engadget" title="Engadget">Engadget</a></i>, DuckDuckGo said that The Pirate Bay and Youtube-dl were never removed from its search results if the user searched for those websites using their name or web address. DuckDuckGo also said there were problems with "site:" <a href="/wiki/Web_search_query" class="mw-redirect" title="Web search query">search queries</a> for these websites and other searches, and that the problem had been fixed.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Fingas-2022&#95;120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fingas-2022-120"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>120<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Associations_with_Microsoft">Associations with Microsoft</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DuckDuckGo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Associations with Microsoft"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In May 2022, a report from <i><a href="/wiki/Bleeping_Computer" title="Bleeping Computer">Bleeping Computer</a></i> by security researcher Zach Edwards found that DuckDuckGo Private Browser allowed Microsoft's trackers to continue running while visiting non-DuckDuckGo websites, unlike Google and Facebook trackers, which were blocked. In response, Weinberg said that "unfortunately, our Microsoft search syndication agreement prevents us from doing more to Microsoft-owned properties. However, we have been continually pushing and expect to be doing more soon." He also said given that most browsers "don't even attempt" to block third-party scripts from loading, users would still be safer than on other browsers.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-allows&#95;56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allows-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-caught&#95;57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-caught-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In August 2022, DuckDuckGo began blocking Microsoft's trackers, saying that the policy preventing them from doing so no longer applied.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-promise&#95;121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-promise-121"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-pushback&#95;58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pushback-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Today, DuckDuckGo continues to open articles through MSN, similar to how Google utilizes AMP.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Criticism_of_Google">Criticism of Google</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DuckDuckGo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Criticism of Google"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In December 2024, DuckDuckGo criticized Google's proposed remedies in an antitrust case related to search engine monopolies. According to DuckDuckGo, the proposal maintains the existing balance of power rather than fostering genuine competition. Gabriel Weinberg, CEO of DuckDuckGo, stated that the proposed measures "attempt to maintain the status quo" and are insufficient to grant smaller players fair access to markets.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>122<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Traffic">Traffic</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DuckDuckGo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Traffic"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:DuckDuckGo_Daily_Traffic_2010-2020.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/DuckDuckGo_Daily_Traffic_2010-2020.png/250px-DuckDuckGo_Daily_Traffic_2010-2020.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="141" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/DuckDuckGo_Daily_Traffic_2010-2020.png/500px-DuckDuckGo_Daily_Traffic_2010-2020.png 1.5x" data-file-width="1378" data-file-height="775" /></a><figcaption>Traffic chart</figcaption></figure>
<p>In June 2013, DuckDuckGo reported a significant traffic increase; according to its <a href="/wiki/Twitter" class="mw-redirect" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> account, on Monday, June 17, 2013, it had three million daily direct searches. On average, during May 2013, it had 1.8 million daily direct searches. Some<sup id="cite&#95;ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>123<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> relate this claim to the exposure of <a href="/wiki/PRISM_(surveillance_program)" class="mw-redirect" title="PRISM (surveillance program)">PRISM</a> and to the fact that other programs operated by the <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Agency" title="National Security Agency">National Security Agency</a> (NSA) were leaked by <a href="/wiki/Edward_Snowden" title="Edward Snowden">Edward Snowden</a>. <a href="/wiki/Danny_Sullivan_(technologist)" title="Danny Sullivan (technologist)">Danny Sullivan</a> wrote on <i>Search Engine Land</i> that despite the search engine's growth "it's not grown anywhere near the amount to reflect any substantial or even mildly notable switching by the searching public" for reasons due to privacy, and he concluded "No One Cares About "Private" Search".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>124<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In response, Caleb Garling of the <i><a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Chronicle" title="San Francisco Chronicle">San Francisco Chronicle</a></i> argued: "I think this thesis suffers from a few key failures in logic" because there had been an increase in traffic and because there was a lack of widespread awareness of the existence of DuckDuckGo.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>125<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2013, the search engine hit 4 million searches per day<sup id="cite&#95;ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>127<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>128<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and in June 2015, it hit 10 million searches per day.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-About&#95;6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In November 2017, DuckDuckGo hit 20 million searches per day.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-About&#95;6-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In January 2019, DuckDuckGo set a record of 1 billion monthly searches;<sup id="cite&#95;ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>129<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and in November of the same year, it hit 50 million searches per day. As of March&#160;2022<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=DuckDuckGo&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, DuckDuckGo was receiving 102,704,358 queries per day on average.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-DDG-traffic&#95;60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DDG-traffic-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On January 11, 2021, a record of over 102.2 million daily searches was achieved.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>130<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A new record of 111,703,299 daily searches was set on 17 January 2022.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-DDG-traffic&#95;60-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DDG-traffic-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2022, DuckDuckGo experienced stagnation and a slight decline in the number of searches per month.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>131<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> At the end of the year 2022, they removed their traffic stats page.
</p><p>Internal surveys by DuckDuckGo found that DuckDuckGo users had a wide variety of <a href="/wiki/Political_spectrum" title="Political spectrum">political leanings</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Thompson-2022&#95;115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thompson-2022-115"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Approximately 56.23% of DuckDuckGo's monthly global traffic comes from the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, 7.01% from <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, 4.95% from the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, 3.93% from <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> and 2.96% from <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>132<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
